  - `MONOPHONIC` means one note total for the whole surface; the highest-priority string wins
  - `STRINGOPHONIC_MONO` means one note per string, using a weighted average along that string
  - `STRINGOPHONIC_POLY` means multiple notes per string, found as local peaks along the string direction
  - `TRACK_FINGERS_ACROSS_STRINGS` keeps a touch matched to the same tracked finger when it slides sideways across strings,
    using the touch-origin metadata. This is opt-in and does not affect surfaces that do not set it.

  `STRINGOPHONIC_ORIGINAL_PLINKY_STYLE` names the existing one-note-per-string behaviour explicitly. */
  int update_from_touch(int x1, int y1, int w, int h, int flags, int max_voices, uint16_t string_mask = 0xffff, int string_pos_offset = 0);
  /* You can also poke in virtual fingers by calling this directly. */
  void poke_finger(int string_idx, int pos_q8, int pressure, int max_voices, bool is_touch = false, bool monophonic = false,
                   int min_pressure_for_note_on = PLAY_SURFACE_PRESSURE_NOTE_ON, uint8_t origin_raw = 255);
  /* If you call `poke_finger(...)` before `update_from_touch(...)`, then the touch will take priority, or vice versa. */

  /* You should call this after updating all fingers, whether via `update_from_touch(...)` or `poke_finger(...)`. */
  void update_voices();

  inline finger_t get_finger_for_voice(int voice) {
    if (voice < 0 || voice >= 16 || ((_used_voices & (1 << voice)) == 0) || _finger_for_voice[voice] >= 16) return finger_t{};
    return fingers[_finger_for_voice[voice]];
  }
  inline int get_finger_origin_y_for_voice(int voice) const {
    if (voice < 0 || voice >= 16 || ((_used_voices & (1 << voice)) == 0) || _finger_for_voice[voice] >= 16) return -1;
    uint8_t origin_raw = _finger_origin_raw[_finger_for_voice[voice]];
    return origin_raw == 255 ? -1 : (origin_raw >> 4);
  }
  inline int get_finger_origin_x_for_voice(int voice) const {
    if (voice < 0 || voice >= 16 || ((_used_voices & (1 << voice)) == 0) || _finger_for_voice[voice] >= 16) return -1;
    uint8_t origin_raw = _finger_origin_raw[_finger_for_voice[voice]];
    return origin_raw == 255 ? -1 : (origin_raw & 15);
  }

  static int get_note_from_position(int relx, int rely, int w, int h, const uint8_t *string_roots, int scale_root, int scale, int flags) {
    int string_idx = (flags & HORIZONTAL) ? rely : relx;
    int num_strings = (flags & HORIZONTAL) ? h : w;
    if (string_idx < 0 || string_idx >= num_strings) return -1;
    int string_root = string_roots[string_idx];
    int pos = (flags & HORIZONTAL) ? relx : h-1-rely;
    return scale_play_surface_note(string_root, pos, scale_root, scale);
  }

  /* do_play_surface is an example high level helper to:
  * draw the surface
  * map positions to notes, using a scale and key, and a tuning for each string

  it calls back for each active note.
  */
  void do_play_surface(int x, int y, int w, int h, int max_voices, uint32_t bg_col, uint32_t root_col, const uint8_t *string_roots,
                       play_surface_note_fn note_fn, void *note_user = nullptr,
                       int flags = VERTICAL | SHOW_BACKGROUND | STRINGOPHONIC_MONO, int scale = 0, int scale_root = -1,
                       scale_play_surface_brightness_fn brightness = nullptr, void *brightness_user = nullptr, int highlight_pitch_class = -1) {
    if (!string_roots) return;
    if (!scale) scale = current_scale;
    if (scale_root < 0) scale_root = current_key;
    int root_mod_12 = (highlight_pitch_class >= 0 ? highlight_pitch_class : scale_root) % 12;
    int string_count = (flags & HORIZONTAL) ? h : w;
    for (int relx = 0; relx < w; ++relx) {
      for (int rely = 0; rely < h; ++rely) {
        int string_idx = (flags & HORIZONTAL) ? rely : relx;
        int string_pos = (flags & HORIZONTAL) ? relx : h - 1 - rely;
        int note = get_note_from_position(relx, rely, w, h, string_roots, scale_root, scale, flags);
        uint32_t col = ((note % 12) == root_mod_12) ? root_col : bg_col;
        if (brightness) col = add_col(col, fade_col(WHITE, brightness(brightness_user, string_idx, string_pos, x + relx, y + rely, note)));
        set_led(x + relx, y + rely, col);
      }
    }
    update_from_touch(x, y, w, h, flags, max_voices);
    update_voices();
    for (int voice = 0; voice < max_voices && voice < 16; ++voice) {
      finger_t finger = get_finger_for_voice(voice);
      if (!finger.pressure || finger.string_idx >= string_count) continue;
      int note = scale_play_surface_note(string_roots[finger.string_idx], finger.fretted(), scale_root, scale);
      int velocity = clampi(touch_pressure_curve_q7(finger.pressure), 1, 127);
      if (note_fn) note_fn(note_user, voice, clampi(note, 0, 127), (uint8_t)velocity, finger);
    }
  }

  void do_play_surface(int x, int y, int w, int h, int max_voices, uint32_t bg_col, uint32_t root_col, int starting_pitch,
                       int interval_degrees, play_surface_note_fn note_fn, void *note_user = nullptr,
                       int flags = VERTICAL | SHOW_BACKGROUND | STRINGOPHONIC_MONO, int scale = 0, int scale_root = -1,
                       scale_play_surface_brightness_fn brightness = nullptr, void *brightness_user = nullptr, int highlight_pitch_class = -1) {
    int string_count = (flags & HORIZONTAL) ? h : w;
    string_count = clampi(string_count, 0, 16);
    uint8_t string_roots[16];
    fill_scale_string_roots(string_roots, string_count, starting_pitch, scale ? scale : current_scale, interval_degrees);
    do_play_surface(x, y, w, h, max_voices, bg_col, root_col, string_roots, note_fn, note_user, flags, scale, scale_root,
                    brightness, brightness_user, highlight_pitch_class);
  }


  // internal:
  void _poke_finger_pads(int string_idx, int pos, int prevp, int p, int nextp, int max_voices, int string_pos_offset,
                         uint8_t origin_raw = 255);
  uint16_t _used_fingers;            // which of the 16 fingers are currently active
  uint16_t _used_strings;            // ...on which strings are the fingers...
  uint16_t _used_voices;             // ...using which voices
  uint16_t _used_fingers_this_frame; // ...and this is built up by update_from_touch and poke_finger.
  uint8_t _finger_origin_raw[16];    // touch-origin byte for each finger when TRACK_FINGERS_ACROSS_STRINGS is in use
  uint8_t _finger_for_voice[16];     // which finger is using each voice.
  uint32_t _next_voice_counter;      // for round robin voice allocation.
  bool _track_fingers_across_strings;
};

int scale_play_surface_note(int string_root_note, int string_pos, int scale_root_note, uint16_t scale);

void draw_scale_play_surface(int x, int y, int w, int h, int flags, const uint8_t *string_root_notes, int string_count,
                             int scale_root_note, uint16_t scale, int highlight_pitch_class, uint32_t col,
                             uint8_t base_brightness = 18, uint8_t highlight_brightness = 96,
                             scale_play_surface_brightness_fn brightness = nullptr, void *brightness_user = nullptr);

/*
### Level-Triggered MIDI Note Declaration

`declare_midi_note(...)` is independent of `play_surface_t`, though the two pair well. In each update where notes are produced,
declare whichever notes should currently be considered "down", with a note number and pressure. Then call `send_declared_midi_notes()`
as a commit marker. The runtime converts that level-triggered state into the correct note on/off/aftertouch messages.
*/
uint8_t declare_midi_note(uint8_t channel, uint8_t note, uint8_t velocity, uint8_t midi_ports = MIDI_PORT_1);
uint8_t declare_midi_note_for_preset_idx(int preset_idx, uint8_t note, uint8_t velocity, uint8_t midi_ports = MIDI_PORT_1,
                                         int midi_channel_wire = -1);

void send_declared_midi_notes(int enable_aftertouch_on_ports = MIDI_PORT_ALL); // aftertouch_ports can be -1 meaning 'same as note_ports'
uint8_t midi_in_note_velocity(uint8_t channel, uint8_t note, uint8_t midi_ports = MIDI_PORT_ALL);
uint8_t midi_out_note_velocity(uint8_t channel, uint8_t note, uint8_t midi_ports = MIDI_PORT_ALL);
typedef void (*midi_note_iter_fn)(void *user, uint8_t channel, uint8_t note, uint8_t velocity, uint8_t midi_ports);
void for_each_midi_in_note(uint16_t channel_mask, uint8_t midi_ports, midi_note_iter_fn fn, void *user = nullptr);
void for_each_midi_out_note(uint16_t channel_mask, uint8_t midi_ports, midi_note_iter_fn fn, void *user = nullptr);

struct surface_midi_t {
  uint8_t channel;
  uint8_t in_ports;
  uint8_t out_ports;
};

/*
Use these as the note and brightness callbacks for play_surface_t::do_play_surface when a surface should act as a MIDI note
controller. Fill surface_midi_t with the channel and input/output port masks, pass the same object as both callback users, and call
send_declared_midi_notes() after drawing. The brightness callback scans both incoming note state and successfully sent output note state.
*/
static inline void send_surface_note(void *user, int voice, int note, uint8_t velocity, finger_t finger) {
  (void)voice;
  (void)finger;
  surface_midi_t *midi = static_cast<surface_midi_t *>(user);
  if (midi) declare_midi_note(midi->channel, (uint8_t)clampi(note, 0, 127), velocity, midi->out_ports);
}

static inline uint8_t surface_note_brightness(void *user, int string_idx, int string_pos, int x, int y, int note) {
  (void)string_idx;
  (void)string_pos;
  (void)x;
  (void)y;
  surface_midi_t *midi = static_cast<surface_midi_t *>(user);
  if (!midi) return 0;
  note = clampi(note, 0, 127);
  uint8_t velocity = maxi(midi_in_note_velocity(midi->channel, (uint8_t)note, midi->in_ports),
                          midi_out_note_velocity(midi->channel, (uint8_t)note, midi->out_ports));
  return velocity ? (uint8_t)(48 + ((int)velocity * 144 + 63) / 127) : 0;
}

/*
## Built-In Synth And Preset Model

The runtime exposes `MAX_SYNTH_PRESETS` voice preset slots plus one mix preset in slot `MIX_PRESET_IDX`.
Public synth helpers in this file use `preset_idx` for those slots. Voices are different: voices are allocated dynamically by you,
and play notes using one of those preset slots.

Each preset has many parameters, each with a stored range. When notes are triggered, the synth chooses values within those ranges.
The four corners of the built-in XY pad provide four related parameter sets that can be interpolated between. Thus, every parameter
actually has 8 values! min and max, times 4 'xy corners'.

Panels can stay fairly simple and still make rich sound by editing presets in `on_ui(...)` and triggering notes from
`on_sequence(...)` via `play_synth(...)`.
*/

/*
### Built-In Synth Voice Control

Use `play_synth(...)` from `on_sequence(...)` or `on_midi(...)` after choosing a voice number. `velocity` is MIDI-style note
velocity in the range 0..127; values outside that range are clamped. `note_q8` is a MIDI note number with 8 fractional bits.

`synth_note_up(...)` is the note-off helper for one voice, and the getter functions expose the current runtime synth state for
LED feedback, meters, or host/controller reporting. Envelope and peak followers use fixed-point ranges:
`get_synth_env_level_q16(...)` returns 0..65535, while preset peak helpers return 0..32767.
*/
void play_synth(int voice, const synth_voice_note_t &note, bool retrigger = false);
void play_synth(int voice, int preset_idx, int velocity, int note_q8, bool retrigger);
void synth_note_up(int voice);
void set_synth_velocity(int voice, int velocity);
int get_synth_velocity(int voice);
int get_synth_note(int voice);
int get_synth_retrigger(int voice);
int get_synth_preset_idx(int voice);
int get_synth_env_level_q16(int voice);
int get_synth_preset_peak_q15(int preset_idx);
int get_synth_preset_peak_channel_q15(int preset_idx, int channel);

const char *midi_note_to_name(int note, bool include_octave, char *buf = nullptr, bool flat = false);

/*
### `play_synth_from_midimsg`

a simple helper to take incoming midi notes on a range of channels and map them to playing voices.
full code provided as an example so that a simple 'route midi to synth' is as simple as calling this routine
but you can see how it works.

midimsg: the incoming midi message
preset_idx: which preset to use. you could for example map CHANNEL_BYTE(midimsg) to this.
prio: allocation priority. a lower-priority note will not steal a higher-priority voice.
subset_start / subset_end: which synth voices this helper may use. `subset_end` is exclusive.
*/
static inline uint32_t make_midi_voice_source_id(uint32_t midimsg) {
  uint32_t port_id = (uint32_t)(HEADER_PORTS(midimsg) >> MIDI_PORT_SHIFT_DOWN);
  return 0x5d000000u | (port_id << 12) | ((uint32_t)CHANNEL_BYTE(midimsg) << 8) | NOTE_NUMBER(midimsg);
}

static inline bool play_synth_from_midimsg(uint32_t midimsg, int preset_idx, voice_allocator_t *voice_allocator, uint8_t prio,
                                           uint8_t subset_start = 0, uint8_t subset_end = MAX_VOICES,
                                           bool treat_aftertouch_as_velocity_update = true) {
  bool aftertouch = IS_AFTERTOUCH(midimsg);
  if (!treat_aftertouch_as_velocity_update) aftertouch = false;
  bool note_on = IS_NOTE_ON(midimsg);
  bool note_off = IS_NOTE_OFF(midimsg);
  if (!note_on && !note_off && !aftertouch) return false;
  if (!voice_allocator) return false;
  if (preset_idx < 0 || preset_idx >= MAX_SYNTH_PRESETS) return false;
  uint8_t note = NOTE_NUMBER(midimsg);
  uint32_t source_id = make_midi_voice_source_id(midimsg);
  int old_voice_idx = voice_allocator->find_voice(source_id, subset_start, subset_end);
  int new_voice_idx = aftertouch ? old_voice_idx
                                 : voice_allocator->voice_allocate(source_id, note_on ? prio : 0, subset_start, subset_end);
  if (new_voice_idx != old_voice_idx) synth_note_up(old_voice_idx);
  uint8_t velocity = note_off ? 0 : NOTE_VELOCITY(midimsg);
  play_synth(new_voice_idx, preset_idx, velocity, note << 8, note_on);
  return true;
}

/*
### Synth Preset Basic MIDI CC Export

`send_synth_cc_out(...)` mirrors one built-in synth preset as outgoing basic MIDI CC messages. It is intended to be called
manually from `on_sequence(...)` by panels that want external gear to see the panel's current synth controls.

`midi_channel_wire` is the exact zero-based wire MIDI channel to send on. Pass `-1` to use the standard system mapping for this
`preset_idx`, which is equivalent to `get_midi_channel_for_preset_idx(preset_idx, true)`.

`ports` is the usual MIDI output bitmask (`MIDI_PORT_1`, `MIDI_PORT_2`, or a combination). `xy_pad_only = true` sends only XY.
`xy_pad_only = false` sends XY plus a rolling round-robin export of the synth parameters.

Current basic CC export is:

  - CC 1 / 2 are the current XY pad position
  - CC 16 + param is the current low value for that parameter at the active XY point
  - CC 44 + param is the current range width (`high - low`) for that parameter

Only changed CC values are transmitted, so it is cheap to call every sequencer tick.
*/
extern "C" void send_synth_cc_out(int ports, int preset_idx, int midi_channel_wire = -1, bool xy_pad_only = false);

/*
### Incoming Basic Synth MIDI CC

`process_midi_message_for_synth_cc(...)` applies the built-in synth's basic incoming CC mapping to one preset slot.

It does not handle NRPN, sysex, MIDI clock, or transport. It normally ignores the MIDI channel embedded in the message and applies
the CC to the requested `preset_idx`.

If `preset_idx == -1`, it uses the standard mapping helper:

`get_preset_idx_for_midi_channel(status & 0x0f, true)`

It currently handles basic CC only, not program change.

preset_idx_write_copies_mask allows you to write to multiple presets at once.
*/
extern "C" bool process_midi_message_for_synth_cc(uint32_t midimsg, int preset_idx = -1, int preset_idx_write_copies_mask = 0);

/*
### Synth Parameter Introspection Helpers

These helpers are useful for advanced panels that want to inspect the built-in synth preset model directly.

`get_synth_param_name(...)` returns the short user-facing name for a synth parameter. Pass `is_mix = true` to look up the global
mix parameters instead of the per-voice parameters.

`get_value_for_param_given_x_y_rnd(...)` answers the question "what actual value would this parameter produce right now?" It takes
the current XY position plus a `rnd_state_t`, then interpolates the preset's low/high range and picks a point inside it.

For `rnd_state_t`, the byte at `vals[param]` acts as the random selector:

  - `0` chooses the low end of the range
  - `255` chooses the high end
  - values in between interpolate linearly

This is the same randomisation model the built-in synth uses internally when it turns preset ranges into concrete note values.
*/
extern "C" const char *get_synth_param_name(int synth_param, bool is_mix);
extern "C" int get_value_for_param_given_x_y_rnd(int synth_param, int slice_idx, int padx, int pady, rnd_state_t *rnd_state,
                                                 const synth_preset_t *preset);

/*
### Help Text Markup

Help text appears in the second-screen view, the emulator, and the IDE. The string is a single line of contextual guidance and it
supports a tiny inline markup DSL:

  - `#rgb` sets a temporary theme-rotated text colour using a 3-digit hex colour such as `#fc2`
  - `##rgb` sets a temporary raw, non-theme-rotated text colour such as `##f33`
  - `#*` turns on bold
  - `#/` turns on italic
  - `#_` turns on underline
  - `#.` resets colour and all style flags back to the default help-text style

Styles are sticky until you reset them, so `#fc2#*Hello#.` means "gold-ish and bold until the reset token".
*/
void set_help_text(const char *str, ...);

extern char panel_folder[17];   // what folder we loaded this panel state from
extern int panel_idx_in_folder; // which panel we loaded within that folder
extern uint8_t panel_hue;       // what the hue is

/*
## File Picker And Save/Load Helpers

The file picker displays two 8x8 blocks side by side:

  - the left half shows folders in alphabetical order
  - the right half shows 64 numbered files inside the current folder

Slots are named as short numbered JSON files such as `00.json`. The same picker machinery is used both for synth presets and for
whole-panel save state.

Loading is intentionally two-stage. The system first applies the load to an inactive panel instance, while the currently running
panel keeps sequencing and audio alive. Before deserialisation, the system clears the staged arena, constructs a fresh panel with
placement-new, initialises its preset storage, and copies the live panel's declared settings into it in memory. The live panel
then receives `on_prepare_staged_load(staged_state)`, which can seed special migration/rehydration state if needed. After
successful deserialisation, `on_serialise(..., reading)` has completed on the staged panel, so any panel-local normalisation can
happen there before the load is made committable. Later, when you call `request_panel_load_finalise()`, the system applies the staged state at the core1 safe point via
`on_commit_staged_load_audio_thread(...)`, followed by the core0 `on_load_finished()` hook. This lets you apply a new state at a
musically sensible moment while keeping main-thread cleanup off the audio core.

Panel-author recipe for deferred, musical-boundary panel loads:

  1. In `on_ui(...)`, only stage the selected file:
     `panel_page.saveload(..., PANEL_PAGE_LOAD_STAGE_ONLY)`.
  2. In `on_sequence()`, if `is_panel_load_staged()` and your chosen boundary has arrived (usually transport stopped
     or the next barline), call `panel_page.picker.request_panel_load_finalise()` and return immediately if it accepts.
     The accepted request suppresses panel sequence/MIDI callbacks until the commit finishes.
  3. In `on_serialise(..., reading)`, rebuild loaded-data invariants and derived tables after fields have been read.
  4. In `on_load_finished()`, reset runtime-only state that was not serialised: playheads, clock dividers, held gates,
     voices, transient UI, and any global state publication the panel owns.
     Panel settings declared in `on_serialise_settings(...)` have already been carried forward by the system.

The following are details of things you dont need to do, but might want to know about:

  1. The first post-load sequence edge is already handled by the shared sequencer primitives. `clock_divider_t::update()`
     re-latches divider state and reports one edge for `has_sequencer_just_loaded()`, and
     normal `playhead_t::update()` calls `sequencer_should_advance_playhead()` to suppress the matching synthetic
     playhead advance. Panels normally should not call `has_sequencer_just_started_or_loaded()` directly; use the
     primitives unless you are managing sequencer-owned counters or switching outside `playhead_t::update()`.
  2. `on_commit_staged_load_audio_thread(...)` is the rare audio-core hook. Use it only when the panel must inspect
     the outgoing live object before the default staged-state copy overwrites it.

The full persistence contract is described in [`save_and_load.h`](#saveandloadh), especially the [`serialiser_t`](#serialisert)
overview and the field-macro section later in that file.
*/
struct file_picker_t {
  hold_timer_t save_timer;
  bool save_action_fired = false;
  int8_t current_folder_idx = -2;
  int8_t current_file_idx = -1;
  int16_t bank_scroll_y = 0;
  int16_t bank_scroll_origin_y = 0;
  int8_t bank_scroll_touch_origin_y = -1;
  int16_t current_bank_cache_cell_idx = -1;
  int16_t caller_bank_cache_cell_idx = -1;
  uint32_t bank_dirs_generation_seen = 0;
  uint8_t current_hue = 0;
  uint8_t preview_pressure = 0;
  uint8_t preview_error = 0;
  uint8_t curx = 0, cury = 0; // current file x/y
  bool current_held = false;
  bool current_pressed = false;
  bool preview_suppressed_by_load_action = false;
  bool want_reset_to_caller = true;
  int8_t delete_requested_file_idx = -1; // -1 means no pending delete

  // cached directory listing
  char cached_root[17];      // eg 'BANKS' or 'CHORDS'.
  char cached_category[17];  // only used for BANKS.
  char bank_category_names[64][17]; // only used for BANKS.
  char folder_names[64][17]; // panel folders, or scratch bank names while scanning BANKS.
  char cached_folder[17];
  uint8_t folder_hues[64]; // panel folder colours, from FOLDERHUES.BIN.
  uint8_t file_colors[64]; // within current_folder
  uint64_t hue_scan_present_mask;
  char cached_icon_folder[17];
  uint8_t cached_icon_rgb[8 * 8 * 3];
  bool cached_icon_valid;
  uint64_t slot_valid_mask;
  uint8_t hue_scan_idx;
  bool hue_scan_active;
  bool has_staged_panel_selection = false;
  int8_t staged_panel_idx = -1;
  uint8_t staged_panel_hue = 0;
  char staged_panel_folder[17];
  int8_t preset_picker_channel = -1;

  // building blocks for file picking.
  void operator()(int main_y, int hue_y, const char *root_folder_name, const char *caller_current_folder_name,
                  int caller_current_file_idx, const char *caller_current_category_name = NULL);
  void on_done(void); // call this when you close the file picker.

  void reset_which_slot_is_selected() {
    want_reset_to_caller = true;
  } // call this eg when opening the file picker. it snaps the current slection to the caller's state.

  bool toggle_delete_selected_slot(int main_y, int file_idx);
  bool is_non_empty_slot_picked(); // returns true if the user picked a non-empty slot. use it to eg light up the load button, or
                                   // gate delete behaviour.

  void make_dirs(void);
  int save_hues(void); // saves hues.bin.
  inline bool is_slot_valid(int idx) const { return idx >= 0 && idx < 64 && ((slot_valid_mask >> idx) & 1); }
  inline void set_slot_valid(int idx, bool value) {
    if (idx < 0 || idx >= 64) return;
    uint64_t mask = (uint64_t)1 << idx;
    if (value)
      slot_valid_mask |= mask;
    else
      slot_valid_mask &= ~mask;
  }

/*
### Preset Convenience Helpers

These wrap the file picker so panels can browse, preview, load, and save synth presets without re-implementing the file UI.
*/
#define FLAG_PICKER_ENABLE_DELETE 1
  int preset_picker(int channel, int main_y, int hue_y, int flags = FLAG_PICKER_ENABLE_DELETE);
  void update_preset_preview(int channel);
  bool can_save_preset_in_this_folder(int channel); // returns true if the current folder is a preset bank that we can save into.
                                                    // use it to eg light up the save button.
  bool is_protected_init_slot(void) const;
  bool is_different_preset_picked(int channel); // returns true if the user picked out a different preset from the current one. use
                                                // it to eg light up the save button.
  bool load_preset_from_selected_slot(int channel, int preset_idx_write_copies_mask = 0, bool dont_touch_xy = false,
                                      const synth_preset_t **loaded_preset_out = nullptr);
  bool save_preset_to_selected_slot(int channel);
  void stop_preset_preview_for_load_action(void);

  // helpers if you want for load / save buttons
  inline uint32_t get_preset_save_button_colour(int channel) {
    if (current_file_idx < 0) return 0;
    if (!can_save_preset_in_this_folder(channel)) return 0;
    if (is_protected_init_slot()) return 0;
    return BRIGHTER(BLUE);
  }
  inline uint32_t get_preset_load_button_colour(int channel) {
    if (!is_non_empty_slot_picked()) return 0;
    return is_different_preset_picked(channel) ? BRIGHTER(GREEN) : GREEN;
  }
  inline uint32_t get_preset_load_save_button_colour(int channel) {
    return get_preset_load_button_colour(channel) | get_preset_save_button_colour(channel);
  }
  /*
  ### Panel Save/Load Helpers

  These are the equivalent file-picker helpers for the panel's own serialized state, rather than individual synth presets.
  */
  int panel_picker(int main_y, int hue_y, int flags = FLAG_PICKER_ENABLE_DELETE);
  bool is_different_panel_picked(
      void); // returns true if the user picked out a different preset from the current one. use it to eg light up the save button.
  bool load_panel_from_selected_slot(void);
  bool save_panel_to_selected_slot(void);

  inline uint32_t get_panel_save_button_colour(void) {
    if (current_file_idx < 0) return 0;
    return BRIGHTER(BLUE);
  }
  inline uint32_t get_panel_load_button_colour(void) {
    if (!is_non_empty_slot_picked()) return 0;
    return is_different_panel_picked() ? BRIGHTER(GREEN) : GREEN;
  }
  inline uint32_t get_panel_load_save_button_colour(void) {
    return get_panel_load_button_colour() | get_panel_save_button_colour();
  }

  /*
  ### Convenience Buttons For Save/Load Dialogs

  These are small ready-made UI helpers for the common "file dialog" button row.

  - `preset_load_button(...)` / `preset_save_button(...)` work on preset slots
  - `panel_load_button(...)` / `panel_save_button(...)` work on full panel state
  - `cancel_button(...)` closes the picker without applying anything
  - `preset_ok_button(...)` / `panel_ok_button(...)` provide the common "OK" behaviour that loads on tap and can optionally save
    on long press
  */
  bool preset_load_button(int channel, int x, int y, int preset_idx_write_copies_mask = 0,
                          const synth_preset_t **loaded_preset_out = nullptr);
  bool preset_save_button(int channel, int x, int y);
  bool panel_load_button(int x, int y);
  bool panel_save_button(int x, int y);
  int cancel_button(int x = 14, int y = 15);
  int preset_ok_button(int channel, bool allow_save_on_long_press, int x = 15, int y = 15,
                       int preset_idx_write_copies_mask = 0,
                       const synth_preset_t **loaded_preset_out = nullptr); // 1=load, 2=save
  int panel_ok_button(bool allow_save_on_long_press, int x = 15, int y = 15);
  bool request_panel_load_finalise(
      void); // queue the staged load for the foreground loop to commit, preserving this picker's folder/index/hue.

  // internal functions
  bool _scan_root_folder(const char *root_folder_name, bool force);
  bool _scan_folder(const char *folder_name, bool force);
  void _load_folder_hues(const char *root_folder_name);
  void _save_folder_hue(int folder_idx);
  void _refresh_folder_icon_cache(const char *folder_name);
  void _scan_one_hue_from_json(void);
  bool _load_selected_preset_for_preview(int channel);
  int _find_folder_index(const char *folder_name);
  int _ok_button(int channel, bool allow_save_on_long_press, int x, int y, int preset_idx_write_copies_mask = 0,
                 const synth_preset_t **loaded_preset_out = nullptr); // 1=load, 2=save
};

inline bool file_picker_t::preset_load_button(int channel, int x, int y, int preset_idx_write_copies_mask,
                                              const synth_preset_t **loaded_preset_out) {
  if (button(x, y, get_preset_load_button_colour(channel), ISOLATED, "Load")) {
    debug_stack_checkpoint_core0(PROFILE_FOURCC("PLD0"));
    bool ok = load_preset_from_selected_slot(channel, preset_idx_write_copies_mask, true, loaded_preset_out);
    debug_stack_checkpoint_core0(PROFILE_FOURCC("PLD1"));
    if (ok) show_warp_load(x, y, GREEN);
    on_done();
    return ok;
  }
  return false;
}

inline bool file_picker_t::preset_save_button(int channel, int x, int y) {
  if (button(x, y, get_preset_save_button_colour(channel), ISOLATED, "Save")) {
    bool ok = save_preset_to_selected_slot(channel);
    if (ok) show_warp_save(x, y, BLUE);
    on_done();
    return ok;
  }
  return false;
}

inline bool file_picker_t::panel_load_button(int x, int y) {
  if (button(x, y, get_panel_load_button_colour(), ISOLATED, "Load")) {
    bool ok = load_panel_from_selected_slot();
    if (ok) show_warp_load(x, y, GREEN);
    on_done();
    return ok;
  }
  return false;
}

inline bool file_picker_t::panel_save_button(int x, int y) {
  if (button(x, y, get_panel_save_button_colour(), ISOLATED, "Save")) {
    bool ok = save_panel_to_selected_slot();
    if (ok) show_warp_save(x, y, BLUE);
    on_done();
    return ok;
  }
  return false;
}

inline int file_picker_t::cancel_button(int x, int y) {
  if (button(x, y, RED, ISOLATED, "Cancel")) {
    on_done();
    return 1;
  }
  return 0;
}

inline int file_picker_t::preset_ok_button(int channel, bool allow_save_on_long_press, int x, int y,
                                           int preset_idx_write_copies_mask,
                                           const synth_preset_t **loaded_preset_out) {
  return _ok_button(channel, allow_save_on_long_press, x, y, preset_idx_write_copies_mask, loaded_preset_out);
}

inline int file_picker_t::panel_ok_button(bool allow_save_on_long_press, int x, int y) {
  return _ok_button(-1, allow_save_on_long_press, x, y);
}

/*
### Whole-Page Preset Example

`preset_pages_t` is a small stateful example of preset-related whole pages:

  - two 16-slider banks, 5 leds high each
  - a 7x5 synth XY pad below them
  - LFO/env buttons and the shared speed control to the right of the pad
  - an optional save/load page using an internally owned file picker

Keep it as a member of your panel, then explicitly place the XY pad with `xy_pad(...)` and call `edit(preset_idx, y)` or
`saveload(preset_idx, y, ...)` for the rest of the page.
*/
struct preset_pages_t {
  slider_t slider_banks[2][16];
  xy_pad_t the_xy_pad;
  file_picker_t picker;

  int edit(int preset_idx, int y, int preset_idx_write_copies_mask = 0, bool include_flag_buttons=true, int slider_flags = 0) { // returns param of first slider touched
    const static int synth_params[32] = {
        VOICE_PARAM_OCTAVE,
        VOICE_PARAM_PITCH,
        VOICE_PARAM_GLIDE,
        VOICE_PARAM_SAMPLE_START,
        VOICE_PARAM_SAMPLE_LENGTH,
        VOICE_PARAM_TIMESTRETCH,
        VOICE_PARAM_CHORUS,
        VOICE_PARAM_SUBOSC,
        VOICE_PARAM_WAVEFOLD,
        VOICE_PARAM_CUTOFF_HP,
        VOICE_PARAM_CUTOFF_LP,
        VOICE_PARAM_RESONANCE,
        VOICE_PARAM_ATTACK,
        VOICE_PARAM_DECAY,
        VOICE_PARAM_SUSTAIN,
        VOICE_PARAM_RELEASE,
        VOICE_PARAM_VOLUME,
        VOICE_PARAM_STEREO,
        VOICE_PARAM_DELAY_SEND,
        VOICE_PARAM_REVERB_SEND,
        VOICE_PARAM_TOAD_FACTOR,
        MIX_PARAM_AUDIO_IN_DRY + 128,
        MIX_PARAM_AUDIO_IN_DELAY + 128,
        MIX_PARAM_AUDIO_IN_REVERB + 128,
        MIX_PARAM_DELAY_TIME + 128,
        MIX_PARAM_DELAY_FEEDBACK + 128,
        MIX_PARAM_REVERB_SHIMMER + 128,
        MIX_PARAM_REVERB_FEEDBACK + 128,
        MIX_PARAM_EQ_BASS + 128,
        MIX_PARAM_EQ_MID + 128,
        MIX_PARAM_EQ_TREBLE + 128,
        MIX_PARAM_OUTPUT_LEVEL + 128,
    };
    // this ordering reflects the same order that toadstep uses, but with
    // both pages compressed onto the same page by using 5-pad high sliders.
    // lower block: main synth params
    int rv1 = synth_param_sliders_block(slider_banks[0], 0, y + 5, 16, 5, preset_idx, synth_params + 0,
                                        preset_idx_write_copies_mask, slider_flags);
    // upper block: fx sends and then the mix parameters
    int rv2 = synth_param_sliders_block(slider_banks[1], 0, y + 0, 16, 5, preset_idx, synth_params + 16,
                                        preset_idx_write_copies_mask, slider_flags);
    if (include_flag_buttons) {
      y+=10;
      synth_flags_button(0, y, preset_idx, SYNTH_FLAG_BUTTON_SIMPLE);
      synth_flags_button(1, y, preset_idx, SYNTH_FLAG_BUTTON_TUNE);
      synth_flags_button(2, y, preset_idx, SYNTH_FLAG_BUTTON_CHOP);
      synth_flags_button(3, y, preset_idx, SYNTH_FLAG_BUTTON_LOOP);
      synth_flags_button(4, y, preset_idx, SYNTH_FLAG_BUTTON_SYNC);
      synth_flags_button(5, y, preset_idx, SYNTH_FLAG_BUTTON_LOWPASS_GATE);
    }
    return (rv1 >= 0) ? rv1 : rv2;
  }

  void xy_pad(int preset_idx, int x = 8, int y = 10, int preset_idx_write_copies_mask = 0,
              bool require_record_button_down_for_speed = false) {
    synth_xy_block(&the_xy_pad, preset_idx, x, y, 7, 5, WHITE, BLUE, false, preset_idx_write_copies_mask,
                   XY_BUTTONS_ON_RIGHT, require_record_button_down_for_speed);
  }

  int saveload_action(int preset_idx, int y, int flags = FLAG_PICKER_ENABLE_DELETE, int preset_idx_write_copies_mask = 0,
                      const synth_preset_t **loaded_preset_out = nullptr) {
    picker.preset_picker(preset_idx, y, y + 8, flags);
    if (picker.cancel_button(14, y + 15)) {
      scroll_to_page(0);
      return -1;
    }
    int action = picker.preset_ok_button(preset_idx, true, 15, y + 15, preset_idx_write_copies_mask, loaded_preset_out);
    if (action)
      scroll_to_page(0);
    return action;
  }

  bool saveload(int preset_idx, int y, int flags = FLAG_PICKER_ENABLE_DELETE, int preset_idx_write_copies_mask = 0) {
    return saveload_action(preset_idx, y, flags, preset_idx_write_copies_mask) != 0;
  }
};

/*
### Whole-Page Panel Example

`panel_page_t` is the matching minimal whole-page example for panel save/load.
*/
enum panel_page_load_mode_t : uint8_t {
  PANEL_PAGE_LOAD_COMMIT_ASAP, // request commit as soon as the system reaches its safe commit point.
  PANEL_PAGE_LOAD_STAGE_ONLY,
};

struct panel_page_t {
  file_picker_t picker;

  static inline void draw_panel_title(int x, int y) {
    leds_draw_bitmap(x, y,
                     "**  *  **  ** * \n"
                     "* *  * * * *  * \n"
                     "**  ** * * ** * \n"
                     "*  * * * * *  * \n"
                     "*  *** * * ** **\n",
                     palette[4][0]);
  }

  bool saveload(int y, bool draw_title = true, int flags = FLAG_PICKER_ENABLE_DELETE,
                panel_page_load_mode_t load_mode = PANEL_PAGE_LOAD_COMMIT_ASAP) {
    picker.panel_picker(y, y + 8, flags);
    if (draw_title) draw_panel_title(0, y + 10);
    if (picker.cancel_button(14, y + 15)) {
      scroll_to_page(0);
      return false;
    }
    int rv = picker.panel_ok_button(true, 15, y + 15);
    if (!rv) return false;
    scroll_to_page(0);
    if (rv != 1) return false;
    if (load_mode == PANEL_PAGE_LOAD_STAGE_ONLY) return true;
    picker.request_panel_load_finalise();
    return false;
  }
};

/*
### Flash-Heavy Loads

Returns true if the currently selected load would need to flash sample data into RP2350 non-volatile storage.

Some presets reference samples that are not yet present in on-chip flash. If a load would need that flash step, audio will have to
pause while the data is committed. This lets a panel detect that disruptive case before it decides when to call
`request_panel_load_finalise()`.
*/
bool is_load_going_to_need_to_flash_some_chunks(void);

===== synth.h =====

typedef struct mix_state_t mix_state_t;

/*
# synth.h

This file defines the data model for Plinky's built-in synth and sampler presets. If you've played with a Plinky panel such
as chords, drums or toadstep, you'll be familiar with most of the concepts in this file from the built-in synth's parameters.

Most panel authors meet these types through `blocks.h`: the runtime exposes `MAX_SYNTH_PRESETS` voice preset slots plus one
global mix preset in slot `MIX_PRESET_IDX`, and the higher-level slider / XY helpers edit the fields defined here. You usually do not need to
manipulate every field directly, but understanding the structure helps when building custom preset editors.

The key idea is that each synth parameter stores a low and high value for each of the four XY corners. At playback time, the
current XY position chooses an interpolated range, and the synth then picks a random value inside that range for each note.

The synth architecture is: there are MAX_SYNTH_PRESETS (12) voice presets; there are MAX_VOICES (12) voices; the panel allocates
those voices itself, then calls `play_synth` for a given voice and chooses a preset idx from 0-11 for that note.
Each voice consists of: a granular sample head, with control over pitch, glide, octave, loop points and loop style;
that sampler reads from a 'tape' loaded into flash memory, managed entirely by the system; its audio is then fed through
optional DSP stages: chorus, a suboscillator, a wavefolder/saturator, a 2 pole highpass filter, a resonant 2 pole lowpass
filter (also linked to envelope by default), an ADSR envelope that drives a 'VCA', and finally a per voice mix stage
that sends the dry signal to the output, plus two send effects: delay and reverb. Notably, the volume parameter uses
its min-and max range not as a randomisation amount, but to control a simple compressor that crushes the dynamic range
of the voice when min!=max.

All the (up to) 12 voices are then summed into the 'dry', 'delay', and 'reverb' busses. this is where the singleton
'mix preset' comes in (typically referenced in code by passing a preset_idx of 12, ie MIX_PRESET_IDX is a valid idx
for preset_idx, when referring to this single mix preset). The mix preset uses the same semantics of 4 XY corners and
random splits on some parameters; but the actual parameter set is quite different, following the MIX_PARAM_ enum below
rather than the SYNTH_PARAM_ enum used by the earlier preset indices.

The mix params control how the live audio input to plinky is mixed with the dry synth sound, the reverb and delay FX returns,
as well as a couple of parameters each for the FX units. The 'tape' refers to a special streaming audio channel that
is used currently only internally, and is best left alone. Eventually this will allow streaming a single 'stem'
from the SD card.

From a panel author's point of view, the parameters in `synth_presets[]` are the primary way to modify the
sound of the built-in synth. This array lives on `panel_t`, and `synth_presets[MIX_PRESET_IDX]` is the global mix preset.
All slots can be edited and managed (and saved and loaded) via a webusb connected webpage, and so largely can
be considered 'read only'.
It is recommended to (at least at first) make use of the preset_pages_t type in blocks.h, which provides UI
for loading, saving, and even editing presets and their parameters.
The next level of granularity would be to provide synth_slider and synth_xy_block calls in the panel's on_ui, to
provide users of your panel with per-parameter control and/or xy pad control over the sound.

*/

/*
## Sample Banks, Slices, And Per-Slice Flags

Each preset has a set of synth parameters, plus up to 8 slices that each point at a region of a sample.
Presets are loaded from named banks, and all presets in one bank share the same underlying sample. You can set this up and audition
it in the [bank editor](sounded.html).

A panel is free to point different presets at different banks. Plinky will then try to load only the needed parts of each bank's
sample data. Because of that, the actual slice start and end addresses should be treated as read-only data loaded from the bank:
panels should not edit them directly, because the sample data for other regions may not be resident.
In other words, preset sample memory management is entirely a system concern, and the right way to get sample data into a panel
is through the preset system.

Each of the 8 slices stores:

  - a note range, for key splits
  - a tune note, representing the slice's natural pitch
  - a chop count used by chop tuning mode
  - packed flags controlling loop mode and pitch behaviour
*/

#define PRESET_DEFAULT_CHOP_COUNT 16

#define VOICE_OPTION_TUNING_MASK 0x3
#define VOICE_OPTION_TUNING_SIMPLE 0 // sample pitch follows playback speed, like a traditional sampler
#define VOICE_OPTION_TUNING_TUNE 1   // detect a fundamental pitch and snap playback back to the played note (wavetable-like use)
#define VOICE_OPTION_TUNING_CHOP 2   // map white notes from the bottom of the note range to equal chunks of the slice
#define VOICE_FLAG_ONESHOT_DEPRECATED 4 // legacy one-shot flag; prefer the loop-mode options above
#define VOICE_FLAG_BPM_STRETCH 8 // force playback to stay in sync with BPM regardless of note pitch
#define VOICE_FLAG_NO_LPGATE 64 // bypass envelope control of the low-pass filter
#define VOICE_FLAG_XY_SYMMETRY 128 // map the physical XY pad around its centre and extrapolate the positive quadrant

#define VOICE_OPTION_LOOPMODE_SHIFT 4
#define VOICE_OPTION_LOOPMODE_MASK (0x3 << VOICE_OPTION_LOOPMODE_SHIFT)
#define VOICE_OPTION_LOOPMODE_LOOP 0              // loop the entire slice
#define VOICE_OPTION_LOOPMODE_ONESHOT 1           // play the slice once and stop
#define VOICE_OPTION_LOOPMODE_LOOP_HALF_XFADE 2   // loop the second half, crossfading against the first half
#define VOICE_OPTION_LOOPMODE_LOOP_QUARTER_XFADE 3 // same idea, but looping only the last quarter
// Legacy aliases kept temporarily while DSP code is migrated.
#define VOICE_OPTION_LOOPMODE_PINGPONG VOICE_OPTION_LOOPMODE_LOOP_HALF_XFADE
#define VOICE_OPTION_LOOPMODE_PINGPONG_HALF VOICE_OPTION_LOOPMODE_LOOP_QUARTER_XFADE

static inline uint8_t voice_option_tuning(uint16_t flags) { return flags & VOICE_OPTION_TUNING_MASK; }
static inline bool voice_option_is_tune(uint16_t flags) { return voice_option_tuning(flags) == VOICE_OPTION_TUNING_TUNE; }
static inline bool voice_option_is_chop(uint16_t flags) { return voice_option_tuning(flags) == VOICE_OPTION_TUNING_CHOP; }
static inline bool voice_option_is_simple(uint16_t flags) { return voice_option_tuning(flags) == VOICE_OPTION_TUNING_SIMPLE; }

static inline uint8_t voice_option_loopmode(uint16_t flags) {
  return (flags & VOICE_OPTION_LOOPMODE_MASK) >> VOICE_OPTION_LOOPMODE_SHIFT;
}
static inline bool voice_option_is_oneshot(uint16_t flags) {
  return voice_option_loopmode(flags) == VOICE_OPTION_LOOPMODE_ONESHOT;
}
static inline bool voice_option_is_loop(uint16_t flags) { return voice_option_loopmode(flags) == VOICE_OPTION_LOOPMODE_LOOP; }
static inline bool voice_option_is_loop_half_xfade(uint16_t flags) {
  return voice_option_loopmode(flags) == VOICE_OPTION_LOOPMODE_LOOP_HALF_XFADE;
}
static inline bool voice_option_is_loop_quarter_xfade(uint16_t flags) {
  return voice_option_loopmode(flags) == VOICE_OPTION_LOOPMODE_LOOP_QUARTER_XFADE;
}
static inline bool voice_option_is_xfade(uint16_t flags) {
  return voice_option_loopmode(flags) >= VOICE_OPTION_LOOPMODE_LOOP_HALF_XFADE;
}
static inline bool voice_option_has_lpgate(uint16_t flags) { return (flags & VOICE_FLAG_NO_LPGATE) == 0; }

static inline bool voice_option_bpm_stretch(uint16_t flags) { return (flags & VOICE_FLAG_BPM_STRETCH) != 0; }
static inline bool voice_option_xy_symmetry(uint16_t flags) { return (flags & VOICE_FLAG_XY_SYMMETRY) != 0; }
static inline void voice_option_rescale_xy_for_flags(uint16_t flags, int *x, int *y) {
  if (!voice_option_xy_symmetry(flags)) return;
  *x = *x * 2 - 128;
  *y = *y * 2 - 128;
}

/*
## Voice Parameters

For each voice parameter, the preset stores a low and high range for each of the four XY corners. On each note, the current XY
position chooses one interpolated low/high pair, and the synth randomises within that range.

Most voice parameters use the usual 0-127 range. Some are bipolar: 64 means a neutral center, and the two halves activate
different behaviours, noted below. `VOICE_PARAM_PITCH` is the main exception: its useful range is wider than the usual 0-127
parameter scale.
*/
enum {
  VOICE_PARAM_CUTOFF_HP,     // Preset CC 16: high-pass filter cutoff
  VOICE_PARAM_CUTOFF_LP,     // Preset CC 17: low-pass filter cutoff
  VOICE_PARAM_RESONANCE,     // Preset CC 18: filter resonance amount
  VOICE_PARAM_ATTACK,        // Preset CC 19: envelope attack time
  VOICE_PARAM_DECAY,         // Preset CC 20: envelope decay time
  VOICE_PARAM_SUSTAIN,       // Preset CC 21: envelope sustain level
  VOICE_PARAM_RELEASE,       // Preset CC 22: envelope release time
  VOICE_PARAM_GLIDE,         // Preset CC 23: pitch glide / portamento time
  VOICE_PARAM_PITCH,         // Preset CC 24: pitch offset (special wider-than-normal range)
  VOICE_PARAM_OCTAVE,        // Preset CC 25: octave transposition
  VOICE_PARAM_SUBOSC,        // Preset CC 26: bipolar: noise below centre, sub oscillator above
  VOICE_PARAM_WAVEFOLD,      // Preset CC 27: bipolar: saturation below centre, wavefolding above
  VOICE_PARAM_STEREO,        // Preset CC 28: stereo spread / width
  VOICE_PARAM_DELAY_SEND,    // Preset CC 29: send amount into delay
  VOICE_PARAM_REVERB_SEND,   // Preset CC 30: send amount into reverb
  VOICE_PARAM_TOAD_FACTOR,   // Preset CC 31: pitch-tracked sample-rate reduction amount
  VOICE_PARAM_VOLUME,        // Preset CC 32: output level for the voice
  VOICE_PARAM_TIMESTRETCH,   // Preset CC 33: sample time-stretch amount
  VOICE_PARAM_SAMPLE_START,  // Preset CC 34: playback start position within the slice
  VOICE_PARAM_SAMPLE_LENGTH, // Preset CC 35: playback length within the slice
  VOICE_PARAM_CHORUS,        // Preset CC 36: bipolar: pitch wobble below centre, chorus above
  VOICE_PARAM_SIDECHAIN_AMOUNT, // Preset CC 37: bipolar: send above centre, duck below centre
  VOICE_PARAM_LAST,
};

/*
## Global Mix Parameters

The global mix parameters control how audio is routed from the individual voices to the final output. They reuse the same synth
parameter structures so they can inherit the same four-corner XY morphing as the per-voice parameters.

`MIX_PARAM_LAST_PAIR` marks the point below which parameters are stored as low/high pairs. For these early mix parameters the pair
is not a per-note randomisation range; instead it describes the operating range of a compressor-style or multiband control.
Parameters after that point are stored as single values.
*/
enum {
  MIX_PARAM_EQ_BASS = 0,     // Mix CC 16: low-band EQ / compressor amount
  MIX_PARAM_EQ_MID,          // Mix CC 17: mid-band EQ / compressor amount
  MIX_PARAM_EQ_TREBLE,       // Mix CC 18: high-band EQ / compressor amount
  MIX_PARAM_TAPE_DRY,        // Mix CC 19: dry tape/sampler return level
  MIX_PARAM_AUDIO_IN_DRY,    // Mix CC 20: dry external audio input level
  MIX_PARAM_LAST_PAIR = MIX_PARAM_AUDIO_IN_DRY,
  MIX_PARAM_TAPE_DELAY,      // Mix CC 21: tape/sampler send into delay
  MIX_PARAM_TAPE_REVERB,     // Mix CC 22: tape/sampler send into reverb
  MIX_PARAM_AUDIO_IN_DELAY,  // Mix CC 23: audio input send into delay
  MIX_PARAM_AUDIO_IN_REVERB, // Mix CC 24: audio input send into reverb
  MIX_PARAM_REVERB_SHIMMER,  // Mix CC 25: shimmer amount in the reverb
  MIX_PARAM_REVERB_FEEDBACK, // Mix CC 26: reverb feedback / sustain
  MIX_PARAM_DELAY_TIME,      // Mix CC 27: delay time
  MIX_PARAM_DELAY_FEEDBACK,  // Mix CC 28: delay feedback amount
  MIX_PARAM_REVERB_RETURN,   // Mix CC 29: wet reverb return level
  MIX_PARAM_DELAY_RETURN,    // Mix CC 30: wet delay return level
  MIX_PARAM_OUTPUT_LEVEL,    // Mix CC 31: final output level
  MIX_PARAM_AUDIO_IN_SIDECHAIN, // Mix CC 32: bipolar audio-input sidechain send/duck amount
  MIX_PARAM_REVERB_SIDECHAIN, // Mix CC 33: bipolar wet reverb return sidechain duck amount
  MIX_PARAM_DELAY_SIDECHAIN, // Mix CC 34: bipolar wet delay return sidechain duck amount
  MIX_PARAM_LAST,
};

/*
## Randomisation State For Synth Parameter Sampling

Many synth helpers choose an actual value by interpolating a low/high pair and then selecting somewhere inside that range.
`rnd_state_t` is the compact "one byte per voice parameter" state used for that choice.

For a given parameter:

  - `0` means "pick the low end of the range"
  - `255` means "pick the high end of the range"
  - values in between interpolate linearly

Most panels never need to touch this directly, but it is useful if you want to ask "what value would this preset actually produce
for this parameter right now?"
*/
typedef struct rnd_state_t {
  union {
    uint8_t vals[VOICE_PARAM_LAST];
    uint32_t vals32[(VOICE_PARAM_LAST + 3) / 4];
  };
} rnd_state_t;

/*
## XY Recording Helpers

The XY pads support recording an LFO-like modulation path, and these are the structures used to store and play back that motion.
*/
#define MAX_XY_RECORDING_LENGTH 256
typedef struct xy_recording_t {
  int8_t xy[MAX_XY_RECORDING_LENGTH][2];
  uint32_t us_per_step;
  int16_t xy_len;
  int8_t minx, maxx;
  int8_t miny, maxy;
  int8_t playing;
  uint32_t start_time_us;
  
} xy_recording_t;

enum {
  MODULATION_SOURCE_A = 0,
  MODULATION_SOURCE_B,
  MODULATION_SOURCE_X,
  MODULATION_SOURCE_Y,
  MODULATION_SOURCE_PRESSURE,
  MODULATION_SOURCE_LAST,
  MODULATION_SOURCE_NONE = -1,
};

enum {
  MODULATION_TARGET_X = VOICE_PARAM_LAST,
  MODULATION_TARGET_Y,
  MODULATION_TARGET_LAST,
};

#define LFO_RECORDING_LENGTH 128
#define MOD_SRC_ATTENUVERTER_DEFAULT 64

typedef struct lfo_recording_t {
  int8_t steps[LFO_RECORDING_LENGTH];
  uint32_t us_per_step;
  uint32_t start_time_us;
  int32_t position;
  uint8_t step_count;
  uint8_t recording;
  uint8_t playing;
  int8_t attenuverter;
} lfo_recording_t;

enum {
  XY_RECORDING_LFO = 0,
  XY_RECORDING_ENV = 1,
  XY_RECORDING_LAST = 2,
};

static inline int get_sanitized_xy_recording_len(const xy_recording_t *lfo) {
 if (!lfo) return 0;
 if (lfo->xy_len <= 0) return 0;
 if (lfo->xy_len > MAX_XY_RECORDING_LENGTH) return MAX_XY_RECORDING_LENGTH;
 return lfo->xy_len;
}

static inline int get_xy_recording_step(uint32_t now, const xy_recording_t *lfo, int shift, bool wrap) {
 int xy_len = get_sanitized_xy_recording_len(lfo);
 if (xy_len <= 0 || lfo->us_per_step == 0) return 0;
 uint32_t elapsed_us = now - lfo->start_time_us;
 uint32_t whole_step = elapsed_us / lfo->us_per_step;
 uint32_t remainder = elapsed_us - whole_step * lfo->us_per_step;
 if (wrap) {
  whole_step %= (uint32_t)xy_len;
 } else if (whole_step >= (uint32_t)xy_len) {
  return ((uint32_t)xy_len - 1) << shift;
 }
 if (shift == 0) return whole_step;
 return (whole_step << shift) + (remainder << shift) / lfo->us_per_step;
}

/*
## `synth_preset_t`

`synth_preset_t` is the full stored state for one preset.

Each preset stores 8 slice descriptors. Each slice packs its sample bounds, tuning, note range, chop count, and flags together
in one struct. Serialization still writes those members as separate arrays so the JSON format stays readable.
*/
typedef struct synth_preset_slice_t {
  uint32_t start_read_only; // System-managed slice boundaries. Do not write to these from panel/user code.
  uint32_t end_read_only; // System-managed slice boundaries. Do not write to these from panel/user code.
  uint16_t tune_q8; // the tune note for this slice.
  uint8_t range_lo;
  uint8_t range_hi;
  uint8_t chop_count;
  uint16_t flags;
} synth_preset_slice_t;

static inline uint8_t preset_slice_chop_count(const synth_preset_slice_t *slice) {
  return slice && slice->chop_count ? slice->chop_count : PRESET_DEFAULT_CHOP_COUNT;
}

static inline bool preset_slice_has_sample_data(const synth_preset_slice_t *slice) {
  return slice && slice->start_read_only < slice->end_read_only;
}

static inline bool preset_slice_has_tune_note(const synth_preset_slice_t *slice) {
  return slice && slice->tune_q8 > 0;
}

static inline bool preset_slice_has_note_range(const synth_preset_slice_t *slice) {
  return slice && ((slice->range_lo != 0) || (slice->range_hi != 0)) && (slice->range_hi >= slice->range_lo);
}

static inline bool preset_slice_is_valid(const synth_preset_slice_t *slice) {
  return preset_slice_has_tune_note(slice);
}

#define PRESET_SLICE_COUNT 8 // max number of slices in one preset

typedef struct synth_preset_t {
  union {
    int16_t corner_params[VOICE_PARAM_LAST][2]
                         [4]; // params for the 4 corners of the xy pad, as min and max values for randomization.
    int16_t corner_params_flat[VOICE_PARAM_LAST * 8];
  };
  int8_t modulation_amount[MODULATION_TARGET_LAST][MODULATION_SOURCE_LAST];
  uint8_t xy[2];
  union {
    xy_recording_t xy_recordings[XY_RECORDING_LAST];
    struct {
      xy_recording_t xy_lfo;
      xy_recording_t xy_env;
    };
  };
  synth_preset_slice_t slice[PRESET_SLICE_COUNT];
  uint8_t last_slice_idx;
  uint32_t tape_length_samples; // not counting the mips etc.; just the base wave tape length.
  uint32_t sample_data_va;  
  char name[17];
  char bank_category[17];
  char bank_filename[17];
  uint8_t preset_in_bank_idx;
  uint8_t hue;
  // Runtime-only flags. These are inferred or managed in memory and are not serialised.
  uint8_t not_been_flashed : 1; // legacy runtime-only field; staged installs now use an explicit request/commit path.
  uint8_t was_cleared_after_error : 1; // real load failed, so this preset was reset to a default fallback.
  uint8_t is_kit : 1; // preset name contains "kit" as a whitespace/_ delimited word.
} synth_preset_t; 

static inline bool preset_uses_proc(const synth_preset_t *preset) {
  return preset && preset->name[0] == '!';
}

static inline bool synth_preset_is_kit(const synth_preset_t *preset) {
  return preset && preset->is_kit;
}

static inline bool preset_has_any_valid_slices(const synth_preset_t *preset) {
  if (!preset) return false;
  for (int i = 0; i < PRESET_SLICE_COUNT; ++i) {
    if (preset_slice_is_valid(&preset->slice[i])) return true;
  }
  return false;
}

static inline int get_suggested_midi_note_q8_for_preset(const synth_preset_t * preset) {
  for (int i=0;i<PRESET_SLICE_COUNT;++i) 
    if (preset->slice[i].tune_q8 > 0) return preset->slice[i].tune_q8;
  return 60<<8; // C4 default if no valid data.
}

typedef struct synth_voice_note_t {
  int note_q8;                   // note in q8 semitones
  int16_t param_override_value;  // same units as preset corner params; for most params 0..127, for pitch q7 semitones
  uint8_t velocity;              // MIDI-style velocity / pressure, 0..127
  int8_t preset_idx;             // 0..MAX_SYNTH_PRESETS-1, SYNTH_VOICE_PRESET_*, or -1 for "unset"
  uint8_t x_override;            // 0..127 overrides preset XY; 255 means "use preset playback XY"
  uint8_t y_override;            // 0..127 overrides preset XY; 255 means "use preset playback XY"
  int8_t param_override_idx;     // VOICE_PARAM_* to override after interpolation, or -1 for none
} synth_voice_note_t;

#define SYNTH_VOICE_PRESET_COLD -2
#define SYNTH_VOICE_PRESET_WARM -3
#define SYNTH_VOICE_PRESET_SEMI_COLD -4
#define SYNTH_VOICE_XY_OVERRIDE_NONE 255
#define PRESET_BANK_DEFAULT_CATEGORY "0_SYNTH"

/*
## Preset Access And XY-Aware Parameter Helpers

Panels usually reach into this file through `blocks.h`, but these are the main low-level access points if you need them directly.
*/
#define MAX_SYNTH_PRESETS 12                                 // number of voice preset slots.
#define MIX_PRESET_IDX MAX_SYNTH_PRESETS                     // the extra preset slot used for global mix parameters.
#define NUM_PRESETS_INCLUDING_MIX (MIX_PRESET_IDX + 1)       // voice presets plus the mix preset slot.

#define mix_preset (synth_presets[MIX_PRESET_IDX])

extern const synth_preset_t cold_synth_preset;

void init_synth_preset(synth_preset_t *preset); // set reasonable values for the preset
void init_semi_cold_synth_preset(synth_preset_t *preset);
void init_mix_preset(synth_preset_t *preset);
bool synth_preset_name_marks_kit(const char *name);
void refresh_synth_preset_runtime_flags(synth_preset_t *preset);
void refresh_synth_preset_modulation_masks(synth_preset_t *preset);
uint32_t get_synth_preset_modulation_target_mask(const synth_preset_t *preset);
uint8_t get_synth_preset_modulation_source_mask(const synth_preset_t *preset);
bool apply_json_string_to_preset(synth_preset_t *preset, const char *json);
bool init_synth_preset_from_json_string(synth_preset_t *preset, const char *json);

/*
### Preset Defaults And Built-In Voice Detection

These helpers expose a small amount of runtime preset policy that panels sometimes need when building custom editors.

`preset_uses_wavetable(...)` tells you whether a preset is currently using the built-in wavetable source rather than a loaded
sample bank.

`get_default_value_for_synth_param(...)` returns the default value for one voice parameter, automatically choosing the wavetable
or sample default set based on the preset you pass.

`get_default_value_for_mix_param(...)` returns the default value for one global mix parameter.

These are intended to avoid panels reaching into internal headers just to query defaults or source mode.
*/
static inline bool bank_filename_uses_wavetable(const char *bank_filename) {
  return bank_filename && (bank_filename[0] == 0 || (bank_filename[0] == '0' && bank_filename[1] == '0'));
}

bool preset_uses_wavetable(const synth_preset_t *preset);
int get_default_value_for_synth_param(const synth_preset_t *preset, int synth_param);
int get_default_value_for_mix_param(int synth_param);
extern int16_t current_mod_source_values_q14[MODULATION_SOURCE_LAST];
extern int8_t current_mod_source_attenuverters[MODULATION_SOURCE_LAST];
extern uint32_t current_modulation_target_mask;
extern uint8_t current_modulation_source_mask;
extern const synth_preset_t *current_modulation_preset_base;
extern uint32_t current_modulation_target_masks[NUM_PRESETS_INCLUDING_MIX];
extern uint8_t current_modulation_source_masks[NUM_PRESETS_INCLUDING_MIX];

/*
### XY-Aware Parameter Read/Write

These helpers are for reading or writing the "effective" parameter range at a particular XY position.

Most higher-level tools should think in terms of the low and high value that a user hears at the current XY pad location, rather
than editing raw corner data directly. These helpers do that interpolation work for you, while keeping the randomisation model
intact.
*/
void get_lo_hi_for_param_given_x_y(int synth_param, int slice_idx, int padx, int pady, int *lo_out, int *hi_out,
                                   const synth_preset_t *preset);
void set_lo_hi_for_param_given_x_y(int synth_param, int slice_idx, int padx, int pady, int loval, int hival,
                                   synth_preset_t *preset);
void add_delta_to_param_for_x_y(int synth_param, int slice_idx, int padx, int pady, int lodelta, int hidelta,
                                synth_preset_t *preset);

/*
### Sample memory access
Samples are managed in terms of chunks of 16384 samples each.
The memory is managed through a kind of 'virtual memory', where a table called chunk_location_ptrs
is used to map from a virtual address (va) into a physical address.
Samples also have a precomputed set of 'mipmaps' - prefiltered octave versions of the original,
used to reduce aliasing when the sample is played at a high pitch.

Each preset has a base virtual address. you can use get_mip_va to find the base
address of any given mip, from 0 (the original sample) upwards (successive octaves) to mip 8.
Given a virtual address, you can then use the macro READ_SAMPLE to read a 16 bit value from memory.
if you try to read a little out of bounds, you will read back silence. If you read beyond
16384 samples past the end of any sample, you may get crashes.

*/
#define READ_SAMPLE(va) chunk_location_ptrs[(va) >> CHUNK_SIZE_SHIFT][(va)]
static inline uint32_t get_mip_va(const synth_preset_t *preset, uint32_t mip, bool force_wavetable);


#define CHUNK_SIZE_SHIFT 14
#define CHUNK_SIZE_SAMPLES 16384
#define CHUNK_SIZE_BYTES (CHUNK_SIZE_SAMPLES * 2)
static_assert(1 << CHUNK_SIZE_SHIFT == CHUNK_SIZE_SAMPLES, "CHUNK_SIZE_SHIFT and CHUNK_SIZE_SAMPLES must match");

#define TAPE_LENGTH_SAMPLES (2 << 21)  // including mips!
#define TAPE_LENGTH_CHUNKS (TAPE_LENGTH_SAMPLES / CHUNK_SIZE_SAMPLES) // including mips
#define TAPE_LENGTH_BYTES (TAPE_LENGTH_SAMPLES * 2)

#define MAX_BANKS MAX_SYNTH_PRESETS

typedef int16_t *  chunk_location_t;
#define MAX_CHUNK_LOCATIONS ((MAX_BANKS+1) * (TAPE_LENGTH_CHUNKS+1)) // +1 for a blank after it.
extern chunk_location_t chunk_location_ptrs[MAX_CHUNK_LOCATIONS];

static inline uint32_t get_mip_va(const synth_preset_t *preset, uint32_t mip, bool force_wavetable) {
  uint32_t mip_offset = 0x200 - (1<<(9-mip));
  uint32_t sample_data_va = force_wavetable ? CHUNK_SIZE_SAMPLES : preset->sample_data_va;
  uint32_t tape_length_samples = force_wavetable ? 65536u : preset->tape_length_samples;
  return sample_data_va + ((tape_length_samples * mip_offset) >> 8);
}

uint64_t pack_param(int synth_param, const int16_t corners[2][4]);
uint64_t get_param_packed(int synth_param, const synth_preset_t *preset); // returns 4 corners and lo and hi values packed into a 64 bit integer. NB doesnt work for pitch!
uint64_t set_param_packed(int synth_param, uint64_t packed, synth_preset_t *preset); // sets the 4 corners and lo and hi values from a 64 bit integer. NB doesnt work for pitch! returns the old value.
void synth_preset_copy_corner_params(synth_preset_t *dst, const synth_preset_t *src); // copies just the corner params and xy pad but leaves the sample settings as is
void set_lo_hi_same_for_all_corners(int synth_param, int loval, int hival, synth_preset_t *preset); // flatten the current XY result into all four corners

static inline int blend4(int a, int b, int c, int d, int x, int y) {
  a = a * 128 + (b - a) * x;
  c = c * 128 + (d - c) * x;
  return (a * 128 + (c - a) * y) >> 14;
}

static inline int blend_int16(const int16_t *src, int x, int y, uint8_t rnd) {
  int min = blend4(src[0], src[1], src[2], src[3], x, y);
  int max = blend4(src[4], src[5], src[6], src[7], x, y);
  return min + (((max - min) * (rnd & 255)) >> 8);
}

void set_xy_for_playback_ex(const synth_preset_t *preset, int *x, int *y, bool include_playback, uint32_t env_start_time_us,
                            uint32_t env_amount_q16);
static inline void set_xy_for_playback(const synth_preset_t *preset, int *x, int *y, bool include_playback) {
  set_xy_for_playback_ex(preset, x, y, include_playback, preset->xy_recordings[XY_RECORDING_ENV].start_time_us, 1u << 16);
}



static inline void copy_corner_param_single(int synth_param, const synth_preset_t *src, synth_preset_t *dst) {
  for (int i = 0; i < 2; ++i) {
    for (int k = 0; k < 4; ++k) {
      dst->corner_params[synth_param][i][k] = src->corner_params[synth_param][i][k];
    }
  }
}

static inline void copy_corner_param_quadrant(int synth_param, int quadrant, const synth_preset_t *src, synth_preset_t *dst) {
  dst->corner_params[synth_param][0][quadrant] = src->corner_params[synth_param][0][quadrant];
  dst->corner_params[synth_param][1][quadrant] = src->corner_params[synth_param][1][quadrant];
}

/*
## `mix_buffers_t`

The global `mix_buffers` structure is the handoff between `panel_t::on_dsp(...)` and the standard Plinky output chain.
It is passed to `on_dsp(...)` as `mix_buffers_out` and is cleared immediately before that hook is called.

Most custom-audio panels fill `dry`, `delaysend`, and `reverbsend`, then let the standard chain run after the hook. That chain
adds delay, reverb, three-band EQ/compression, and output level using parameters from the mix preset in
`synth_presets[MIX_PRESET_IDX]`.

If you are not using the standard FX path, you are free to use the memory in `mix_buffers_t` for your own purposes. Note that the
delay buffer is stored in PSRAM, and is therefore slower to access than the reverb or dry buffers.
*/

#define REVERBBUF_SAMPLES 32768  // 64k of fast ram. mono.
#define DELAYBUF_SAMPLES 65536 // 256kb of psram!. stereo.

/*
Return the PSRAM-backed delay buffer used by the standard delay. Access it carefully from DSP code; PSRAM is slower than normal
RAM and should not be treated as a cheap random-access scratch buffer.
*/
int16_t *get_psram_delay_buf(void);

typedef struct mix_buffers_t {
  int16_t reverbbuf[REVERBBUF_SAMPLES]; // used by the plinky reverb
  int dry[BLOCK_SIZE * 2];
  union {
    struct {
      int delaysend[BLOCK_SIZE]; // half sample rate
      int reverbsend[BLOCK_SIZE]; // half sample rate
      short tempshort[BLOCK_SIZE]; // use it how you like 
      int voice_mix_input[BLOCK_SIZE * 2]; // stereo handoff into do_voice_mix
    };
    float _lroutput[BLOCK_SIZE * 6]; // used internally (aliased with above)
  };
} mix_buffers_t;
extern mix_buffers_t mix_buffers;

/* 
### `do_mix`

the system mix runs when `on_dsp(...)` returns `false`, after dry, delay and reverb sends have been filled in `mix_buffers_out`.
The dry path is full-rate stereo. The delay and reverb send paths are lower-rate send buffers shaped by the struct below.

Panels that need to own final audio output can override `on_dsp(...)`, write final interleaved stereo samples to `audiobuf_out`,
and return `true`. The advanced `on_dsp_core0_final_mix_unsafe(...)` hook runs on core 0 from the high-priority audio-footer
doorbell inside `do_fx()`; it is for tiny bounded stock-panel final tweaks only.
*/
void do_mix(int16_t *inputbuf, int16_t *outputbuf); 

/*
### `do_reverb`

if you want to use the plinky12 reverb without the rest of the mix chain,
you can call do_reverb to process one sample. it is intended to be run at 16khz ie
half sample rate. you feed it a stereo signal and it *accumulates* onto a stereo output.
be sure to initialize wetl and wetr (eg to zero) before calling this.

the reverb uses the memory in mix_buffers.reverbbuf.
it is called internally by do_fx.
*/
void do_reverb(int reverbinl, int reverbinr, int reverb_size_q7, int *wetl, int *wetr);
extern int reverb_extra_fb_gain_q8;
extern int reverb_extra_shimmer;

/*
### `do_delay`

if you want to use the plinky12 delay without the rest of the mix chain,
you can call do_delay to process one sample. it is intended to be run at 16khz ie
half sample rate. you feed it a stereo signal and it *accumulates* onto a stereo output.

the delay_time_q16 is in samples (with 16 bits of fractional precision).
delay_fb_cos_q12 (and sin) are 12 bit fractional, and the stereo image is 'rotated'
by the angle implied by the cos and sin. if you want no rotation, just put the feedback
amount in cos and leave sin 0.

the delay uses the last 256kb of PSRAM.
it is called internally by do_fx.
*/
void do_delay(int delay_send_l, int delay_send_r, int delay_time_q16, int delay_fb_cos_q12, int delay_fb_sin_q12, int *wetl, int *wetr);

===== save_and_load.h =====

/*
# save_and_load.h

This file is the panel save/load API.

Panels save their durable state as JSON. The system owns the file picker UI, SD card I/O, and the mechanics of calling your
serialiser. Your panel's job is to decide which fields matter, write them in `on_serialise(serialiser_t&, int version)`, and keep
final commit work small. If loaded data needs normalising or derived indexes rebuilt, do that at the end of `on_serialise(...)`
when `s.reading` is true.

The normal pattern is:

  1. implement `get_version()` so you can evolve old save files when needed
  2. implement `on_serialise(...)`
  3. inside `on_serialise(...)`, describe your state with `OBJECT_BEGIN`, `FIELD`, `FIELD_ARRAY`, and friends

Example:

```cpp
bool my_panel::on_serialise(serialiser_t &s, int version) {
  OBJECT_BEGIN(s);
  FIELD("step", step_index);
  FIELD("name", name);
  FIELD_ARRAY("notes", notes, note_count);
  OBJECT_END(s);
  return true;
}
```

Panels that keep large buffers in PSRAM can append a binary footer to the same panel save file without base64 overhead. Call
`serialise_psram_binary_footer(s, codec, offset, length)` after your top-level `OBJECT_END(s)` in `on_serialise(...)`. The JSON
root is still valid JSON up to its final `}`; the save code then appends a footer of the form `\n//CCC00000000:` followed by
binary data, where the three-character tag names the codec and the eight hex digits are the uncompressed byte count. Current
firmware implements the `BIN` passthrough codec, the `ZER` zero-run codec, and the `AUD` lossy stereo PCM codec. `ZER` stores
signed 16-bit run lengths counted in 32-bit dwords, so its PSRAM range must be dword-aligned. `AUD` stores stereo-frame-aligned
int16 PCM as 128-frame blocks of two predicted 8-bit residual streams, with a compact silence marker for all-zero blocks. The
save call's codec argument only affects writing; loading dispatches from the file's footer tag.

Field names are the JSON keys. They do not need to match your C/C++ field names, but they should stay short and stable. Keys are
hashed from at most 16 characters, so prefer compact names and do not rely on long names being distinct.

This serialiser is intentionally small and fixed-shape:

  - fixed-size C arrays are the normal model
  - fixed-size strings are the normal model
  - object fields are declared explicitly
  - dynamic allocation is not the intended pattern

The load flow is intentionally two-stage:

  - the running panel continues to sequence and produce audio
  - a second, inactive copy is used as the load target
  - only when you choose to "commit" the load does the running panel copy useful state across

In practice:

  - on boot, the live panel is zeroed, constructed, its presets are initialised, panel settings are loaded from SD, then
    `setup_default_panel_state()` runs
  - `setup_default_panel_state()` builds the default user-facing panel/song used at startup and by the blank-panel load action
  - when loading a saved panel, the inactive arena is zeroed, constructed, and given default preset storage
  - the live panel's declared settings are copied into the inactive panel in memory, without SD or JSON I/O
  - the live panel then receives `on_prepare_staged_load(staged_state, panel_memory_size)` for rare migration/rehydration setup
  - after that short preparation step, the file is deserialised into the inactive panel while the live panel can keep sequencing
  - when loading the "init" slot (`00:0`), the inactive panel receives the live panel settings, then runs
    `setup_default_panel_state()` instead of deserialising from disk
  - later, when the panel calls `request_panel_load_finalise()`, core1 applies the staged copy via
    `on_commit_staged_load_audio_thread(loaded_state)`, then core0 runs `on_load_finished()` for final runtime followup work

This separation keeps durable saved state, derived staged data, startup-only defaults, and final runtime timing state distinct.

If you are coming here from the panel helpers in `blocks.h`, the user-facing file UI is documented there in
[`File Picker And Save/Load Helpers`](#file-picker-and-saveload-helpers). This file is the lower-level contract that actually
serialises the durable state.
*/

/*
## Tempo Save/Load Helper

Panels sometimes want to persist the current tempo as part of their top-level musical state, but they usually do **not** want to
persist the current clock source. A saved panel should not silently switch the transport away from an external CV or MIDI clock.

For that case, use `serialise_tempo(...)` for a JSON field that represents the global quarter-note period in microseconds.
for example, inside your panel's on_serialise, you can write

```c
FIELD_FN("clock_period", serialise_tempo);
```

On save, it writes the current global transport tempo. On load, it applies the loaded value back to the global transport only if
the current clock source is already internal; if the system is currently following CV or MIDI clock, the loaded value is ignored.

Because tempo is global transport state rather than panel-owned state, queued panel loads stage this value and apply it when the
load is committed. Other deserialisation paths apply it directly.
*/
bool serialise_tempo(struct serialiser_t &s);
struct calibration_data_t;
bool serialise_calibration_data(struct serialiser_t &s, struct calibration_data_t &o);

#define _noinline __attribute__((noinline))

// 16 character max hash for field names; executes entirely at compile time so it can be used in a switch statement.
#define UC(lit, i) (((uint64_t)(unsigned char)((lit)[i])) << (i * 8))
#define UC8(x) (UC(x, 0) + UC(x, 1) + UC(x, 2) + UC(x, 3) + UC(x, 4) + UC(x, 5) + UC(x, 6) + UC(x, 7))
#define HASH_(x) (UC8(x) + UC8(x + 8) * 1327217884ull)
#define HASH(lit) (HASH_(lit "                ")) /* 16 spaces */

static inline uint64_t literal_hash_span(const char *s, const char *e) {
  char buf[17] = "                ";
  memcpy(buf, s, (e - s) < 16 ? (e - s) : 16);
  return HASH_(buf);
}

static inline int hex_digit_value(char c) {
  if (c >= '0' && c <= '9') return c - '0';
  if (c >= 'a' && c <= 'f') return 10 + (c - 'a');
  if (c >= 'A' && c <= 'F') return 10 + (c - 'A');
  return -1;
}

/*
## `serialiser_t`

`serialiser_t` is the low-level reader/writer.

Most panels should not call these methods directly beyond passing the object into `serialise(...)` helpers. The main authoring
surface is the set of `serialise(...)` overloads plus the field macros near the end of this file.
*/
struct serialiser_t {
  static constexpr uint32_t bufsize = 256;
  static constexpr uint32_t scratch_extra = 4;
  static constexpr char hexdigits[] = "0123456789abcdef";
  char buf[bufsize + scratch_extra];
  FIL *f;
  const char *memory;
  const uint8_t *copy_src_base;
  uint8_t *copy_dst_base;
  uint32_t copy_length;
  uint32_t memory_length;
  uint32_t memory_pos;
  uint32_t pos;
  uint32_t valid;
  uint32_t is_array_bitmask;
  uint64_t byte_offset_of_buf;
  uint32_t line_of_buf;
  uint32_t binary_footer_psram_offset;
  uint32_t binary_footer_length;
  void *panel_context;
  uint8_t depth; // max 32
  char binary_footer_codec[4];
  const char *active_field_key;
  FRESULT write_result;
  UINT write_error_expected;
  UINT write_error_actual;
  bool trailing_comma;
  bool reading;
  bool eof;
  bool binary_footer_requested;

  void init_common(bool _reading) {
    pos = depth = valid = 0;
    is_array_bitmask = 0;
    trailing_comma = false;
    active_field_key = NULL;
    reading = _reading;
    eof = false;
    write_result = FR_OK;
    write_error_expected = 0;
    write_error_actual = 0;
    byte_offset_of_buf = 0;
    line_of_buf = 1;
    panel_context = NULL;
    binary_footer_psram_offset = 0;
    binary_footer_length = UINT32_MAX;
    memcpy(binary_footer_codec, "BIN", 4);
    binary_footer_requested = false;
    memset(buf, 0, sizeof(buf));
  }

  void init(FIL *fi, bool _reading) {
    f = fi;
    memory = NULL;
    copy_src_base = NULL;
    copy_dst_base = NULL;
    copy_length = 0;
    memory_length = 0;
    memory_pos = 0;
    init_common(_reading);
    if (reading) fill();
  }

  void init_from_memory(const char *text) {
    f = NULL;
    memory = text ? text : "";
    copy_src_base = NULL;
    copy_dst_base = NULL;
    copy_length = 0;
    memory_length = (uint32_t)strlen(memory);
    memory_pos = 0;
    init_common(true);
    fill();
  }

  void init_memory_copy(void *dst_base, const void *src_base, uint32_t length) {
    f = NULL;
    memory = NULL;
    copy_src_base = (const uint8_t *)src_base;
    copy_dst_base = (uint8_t *)dst_base;
    copy_length = length;
    memory_length = 0;
    memory_pos = 0;
    init_common(false);
  }

  inline bool memory_copying() const { return copy_src_base != NULL && copy_dst_base != NULL; }
  inline bool write_ok() const { return write_result == FR_OK; }

  _noinline bool note_write_error(FRESULT result, UINT requested, UINT written) {
    if (write_result == FR_OK) {
      write_result = (result != FR_OK) ? result : FR_DISK_ERR;
      write_error_expected = requested;
      write_error_actual = written;
    }
    printf("serialiser write error: res=%d bytes=%u/%u\n", (int)write_result,
           (unsigned)write_error_actual, (unsigned)write_error_expected);
    return false;
  }

  _noinline bool copy_field(void *dst, uint32_t length) {
    if (!memory_copying()) return false;
    uintptr_t dst_addr = (uintptr_t)dst;
    uintptr_t base_addr = (uintptr_t)copy_dst_base;
    if (dst_addr < base_addr || dst_addr - base_addr > copy_length || length > copy_length - (uint32_t)(dst_addr - base_addr)) {
      printf("memory copy serialiser error: field is outside destination object\n");
      return false;
    }
    uint32_t offset = (uint32_t)(dst_addr - base_addr);
    if (length > 0) memcpy(dst, copy_src_base + offset, length);
    return true;
  }

  bool flush() {
    if (memory_copying()) {
      pos = 0;
      return true;
    }
    UINT nwritten = 0;
    if (!reading && pos) {
      if (f) {
        FRESULT result = f_write(f, buf, pos, &nwritten);
        // #ifndef NDEBUG
        //       fwrite(buf, 1, pos, stdout);
        // #endif
        if (result != FR_OK || nwritten != pos) {
          UINT requested = (UINT)pos;
          pos = 0;
          return note_write_error(result, requested, nwritten);
        }
      } else if (forward_bytes_to_webusb_host) {
